<div id="review_98983992" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/98983992" />
    <a title="Heather" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1802220-heather"><img alt="Heather" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1400204513p2/1802220.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/98983992?book_show_action=true">Apr 17, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heather" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heather" href="/user/show/1802220-heather">Heather</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1802220-heather?shelf=ya-romance-to-everything-in-between">ya-romance-to-everything-in-between</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1802220-heather?shelf=books-read-in-2010">books-read-in-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1802220-heather?shelf=ya-galley-books">ya-galley-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer98983992" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11763319565532473302">I can't help it, but I love cutesy YA romantic books- that's why I ended up giving this three stars. It was a fast read, thank goodness, because I really detested (strong word I know, but that's how I felt) the writing style. <br/><br/>I'm from California and I use the words "like" and "really" a lot. I would probably be really (ha, see) embarrassed if I went back and read a lot of my reviews. I'm sure I would see those words everywhere. But, they are only reviews. These words were used obsessively. I sta</span>
  <span id="freeText11763319565532473302" style="display:none">I can't help it, but I love cutesy YA romantic books- that's why I ended up giving this three stars. It was a fast read, thank goodness, because I really detested (strong word I know, but that's how I felt) the writing style. <br /><br />I'm from California and I use the words "like" and "really" a lot. I would probably be really (ha, see) embarrassed if I went back and read a lot of my reviews. I'm sure I would see those words everywhere. But, they are only reviews. These words were used obsessively. I started to roll my eyes at one point. Anyway, the language was overdone. In addition, the phrasing "I was like" and "I say" for introducing who said what, was way over used as well. Annoying...<br /><br />I know this is an advanced readers copy and I haven't read anything from this author before, but I couldn't image too much being changed, with that being said, the writing lacked for me (as I've already stated). Once again, I hate to degrade the YA readership by saying they might be okay with this writing style. It's probably true though. <br /><br />I did think this was cute, but it was the same old same old story once again. Friends like the same boy, friends fight, and then all is well in the world at the end. Ordinary...<br /><br />Because of my cork for not being able to finish a book once I started it, I ended up reading this super fast, just so I could be done with it. That doesn't sound good after just rereading that sentence. It's true though. Some would say I wasted my time, especially because I wont remember it probably a week from now. It's sad really. <br /><br />I'm going on and on I'm sorry. I know it sounds like I really hated this book, but I didn't. I just didn't care for the writing (I've said that about the writing like...ha... how many times now... annoying isn't it) and that means something. The writing is essential, not all, but important to the connection and how we care about the characters and their stories. <br /><br />I'm done ranting now... promise. </span>

<div id="review_137341365" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/137341365" />
    <a title="Emily" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4724954-emily"><img alt="Emily" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/137341365?book_show_action=true">Dec 30, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily" href="/user/show/4724954-emily">Emily</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4724954-emily?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer137341365" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3335474580312897649">Initially, I was really excited to read this book. I had just finished a book with a similar premise (The Unwritten Rule by Elizabeth Scott), so I was interested in seeing how this one would be different.<br/><br/>Unfortunately, I was not impressed. The love triangle premise has been done to death, so it was really disappointing that Ms. Colasanti didn't do much to spice it up. Maybe adding Lani's obsession with fate to the mix was her way of trying to create a different path, but in the end, that storyli</span>
  <span id="freeText3335474580312897649" style="display:none">Initially, I was really excited to read this book. I had just finished a book with a similar premise (The Unwritten Rule by Elizabeth Scott), so I was interested in seeing how this one would be different.<br /><br />Unfortunately, I was not impressed. The love triangle premise has been done to death, so it was really disappointing that Ms. Colasanti didn't do much to spice it up. Maybe adding Lani's obsession with fate to the mix was her way of trying to create a different path, but in the end, that storyline just dragged on and on. Lani was obsessed with reading her horoscope and, of course, her horoscopes always applied to whatever situation she was in. Which leads me to my next annoyance: Jason and Lani have too much in common, and I'm not talking about sharing favorite poptarts or anything like that. It's obscure things, like how they compare brands of water to shapes/colors. For instance, they think one brand of water tastes like orange rhombus, while another tastes like red circle. What does that even mean? Definitely was rolling my eyes at that part.<br /><br />Another problem I had was with the dialogue style. There were multiple pages where it was pretty much nothing but back and forth, short dialogue without much indication who was saying what. And Lani did a lot of this in her narration:<br /><br />Erin was like, "Blah blah blah."<br />Then Jason goes, "Blah blah blah."<br />And I was all, "Blah blah blah."<br /><br />I understand that a lot of teenagers talk like that, but it was really annoying to read it in narration like that.<br /><br />The only two characters I liked were Connor and Blake, but even then they were barely in the novel, which was disappointing. Perhaps they had been featured more, I could have better enjoyed the book.<br /><br />Overall, the writing was basic, the characters were basic, and, of course, the premise was basic.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3335474580312897649" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_598543886" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/598543886" />
    <a title="Abbie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8835818-abbie"><img alt="Abbie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514031899p2/8835818.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/598543886?book_show_action=true">Apr 23, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Abbie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Abbie" href="/user/show/8835818-abbie">Abbie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Abbie by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/8482982-adrienne">Adrienne</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8835818-abbie?shelf=ebooks">ebooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8835818-abbie?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer598543886" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15171827217245346235">This book was okay. It was a love triangle theme with lots of typical high school drama. I just didn't really like the characters because they weren't that relatable. <br/><br/>Lani and Erin were best friends who shared a tragic past -- they were in a car accident together and Erin had saved Lani's life. So they were really close. Plus, they were quite obsessed with the idea of fate and destiny; meaning that they liked astrology, palm reading, tarot cards and etc.They also had a gay friend named Blake but</span>
  <span id="freeText15171827217245346235" style="display:none">This book was okay. It was a love triangle theme with lots of typical high school drama. I just didn't really like the characters because they weren't that relatable. <br /><br />Lani and Erin were best friends who shared a tragic past -- they were in a car accident together and Erin had saved Lani's life. So they were really close. Plus, they were quite obsessed with the idea of fate and destiny; meaning that they liked astrology, palm reading, tarot cards and etc.They also had a gay friend named Blake but nobody but Lani knows about it because Blake's dad is super strict.<br /><br />Anyway, in typical love triangle fashion Erin liked this boy named Jason who had an instant connection with Lani (why is it always so fast?). Blake knew about it and so did the rest of the school because they were pretty close (and they hung out in public everyday. If I were Erin I'd be suspicious already). Over the summer Jason broke up with Erin and professed his love for Lani. Uh, there was this whole guilt thing so Lani wasn't very eager to go out with her best friend's ex (You feel guilty now?). Jason sent Erin an explanation letter about him and Lani... then a nasty fight ensued (the dude breaks up with Erin through a letter and tries to explain how he's in love with her best friend in a letter too? I don't like him).<br /><br />But after a very public display of affection Erin forgave Lani and Jason (she can't really do anything about it). And they all lived happily ever after (typical).<br /><br />I wish I liked it more but it was very predictable. And in my opinion it seemed that the supposedly high school students acted like a bunch of kids because of their closed-minded reactions. Even Lani seemed like she wasn't in high school sometimes. And I didn't really enjoy the "sweet" moments between Lani and Jason. But for people who like love triangles and fate, this would be a book you'd enjoy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15171827217245346235" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_77603403" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Princess Bookie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1218813-princess-bookie"><img alt="Princess Bookie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1243916881p2/1218813.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/77603403?book_show_action=true">Nov 12, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Princess Bookie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Princess Bookie" href="/user/show/1218813-princess-bookie">Princess Bookie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1218813-princess-bookie?shelf=read2010">read2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer77603403" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16980554229951332460">My Thoughts: I have been looking forward to this book for months, as most of you know from my blog posts about this book!!! We meet Jason, Lani, and Erin. Erin is dating Jason but Lani has liked him for a while. Lani feels, "why would Jason want an ordinary girl like her, when he can have gorgeous Erin?" Erin is usually the one who gets all the boyfriends. We can tell from the way Jason looks at Lani, he likes her too. The three of them spend lots of time together and the intense eye contact bet</span>
  <span id="freeText16980554229951332460" style="display:none">My Thoughts: I have been looking forward to this book for months, as most of you know from my blog posts about this book!!! We meet Jason, Lani, and Erin. Erin is dating Jason but Lani has liked him for a while. Lani feels, "why would Jason want an ordinary girl like her, when he can have gorgeous Erin?" Erin is usually the one who gets all the boyfriends. We can tell from the way Jason looks at Lani, he likes her too. The three of them spend lots of time together and the intense eye contact between Lani and Jason, you can see the chemistry that is brewing between them. Lani doesn't want to hurt Erin because Erin feels like a "sister" to her and she doesn't know what to do about her feelings. Erin ends up going out of town for a while so Lani and Jason get to know each other better as friends. Things slowly progress between them. What happens to Lani and Jason? What about Erin? I loved this book so much. Everything about it was amazing. The writing, the chemistry between the two characters. Susane has done it again!!! One word, amazing!<br /><br />Overall: Amazing!!! Loved Jason from the first moment we meant him. You could see he was one of a kind and was a great guy.<br /><br />Cover: Loved it. Instantly attracts you to it! Love the way they are holding hands behind the couch, and I love how the colors all go together. Even the girl's hair looks pretty in the ponytail. Come on, even the guy's arm is hot!!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="16980554229951332460" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Sana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5862550-sana"><img alt="Sana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557438942p2/5862550.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/188516062?book_show_action=true">Jul 24, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sana" href="/user/show/5862550-sana">Sana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781101223000" href="/book/show/8461505-something-like-fate">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5862550-sana?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer188516062" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7919495579881899863">I have been waiting to get my hands on Something Like Fate since I got to know that it is more or less similar to The Unwritten Rule by Elizabeth Scott, which I truly loved. It was good to read the book and I look forward to reading more by Susan Colasanti.<br/><br/>Provided that Something Like Fate had 17 years old protagonists, it rather had a 15-year-olds feelings attached to it. The way Susan Colasanti handled the feelings of Lani and Erin were inferior to that of Jason and Blake. Apart from that, I w</span>
  <span id="freeText7919495579881899863" style="display:none">I have been waiting to get my hands on Something Like Fate since I got to know that it is more or less similar to The Unwritten Rule by Elizabeth Scott, which I truly loved. It was good to read the book and I look forward to reading more by Susan Colasanti.<br /><br />Provided that Something Like Fate had 17 years old protagonists, it rather had a 15-year-olds feelings attached to it. The way Susan Colasanti handled the feelings of Lani and Erin were inferior to that of Jason and Blake. Apart from that, I was really hoping for an ending that builds up slowly rather than a bolt of lighting type of ending.<br /><br />However, I really liked the way the relationship between Lani and Jason develops. It is just so content and mutual that it all just seems to perfect. The whole insertion of Blake and Connor were also perfectly balanced within the book. It gave a singsong quality to the overall theme of the book.<br /><br />Another refreshing addition to the book was the environmentalist side of Lani. It is really good to read about such people who care about the environment so intensely.<br /><br />Overall, it had a little bit of fierce feeling missing from it. And it was kind of wrong for Lani to think that Erin has the power to control her life only 'cause she owes her. But then, to each his own.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7919495579881899863" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer321868740" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14966750695416148271">Reading this book was so interesting. I give this 4 stars because threw out the whole book it made you just want to keep on reading. It was about two bestfriends who were always close to eachother and than one of them meets a boy. When she starts talking to him the other bestfriend starts noticing that he acts different but only around her. What makes you keep reading is when the best friend who is with the guy leaves to a trip she trusts the other bestfriend to be with him back at home. Well wh</span>
  <span id="freeText14966750695416148271" style="display:none">Reading this book was so interesting. I give this 4 stars because threw out the whole book it made you just want to keep on reading. It was about two bestfriends who were always close to eachother and than one of them meets a boy. When she starts talking to him the other bestfriend starts noticing that he acts different but only around her. What makes you keep reading is when the best friend who is with the guy leaves to a trip she trusts the other bestfriend to be with him back at home. Well when she returns she finds out that they had an affair. What realy happened was he liked her bestfriend and they felt like it was fate simply because they understood eachother so well. Because she felt bad for doing that behind her best friends back, she stops talking to him even though it kills her inside. At the end she all she can really do is tell her bestfriend sorry but it just happened. It wasen't after all because fate put them together but because they were right for eachother and that eventually her bestfriend would have to accept it sooner or later. I loved this book because it related very well with my high school years so far and if I could I would reccommend this to many girls who have an interest in boys and bestfriend problems.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14966750695416148271" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer997009206" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12411787379491302283">I was very excited to read this book as a nice little enjoyment for summer. Boy oh boy.... No matter what, if I start to read some thing, I have to finish it. I was very close to just ending the book in the middle, but I had to keep telling myself to finish it so my money wasn't wasted.<br/><br/>Don't get me wrong, the storyline was great! It had so much potential. But I felt like the first person style and the writing made me feel like I was, 'like, a total valley giiirllllll'. <br/><br/>Also, the story was extrem</span>
  <span id="freeText12411787379491302283" style="display:none">I was very excited to read this book as a nice little enjoyment for summer. Boy oh boy.... No matter what, if I start to read some thing, I have to finish it. I was very close to just ending the book in the middle, but I had to keep telling myself to finish it so my money wasn't wasted.<br /><br />Don't get me wrong, the storyline was great! It had so much potential. But I felt like the first person style and the writing made me feel like I was, 'like, a total valley giiirllllll'. <br /><br />Also, the story was extremely predictable so it was very hard to want to keep reading. Especially if you've been right about what's about to happen even 3/4 through.<br /><br />Anyway, I finished the book just so I could put it on my 'Finished Reading' bookshelf at home.<br /><br />I also started reading the little excerpt to Susane's book at the very back thinking that maybe the writing style was purposefully like that.<br /><br />Nope. Not at all. <br /><br />Just the writing style and the predictability was what really set this book low for my rating.</span>

		<td>
		    <b>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('KbwoQbTTx1PVqgkxFeT35xF7sgQTvKtxWQkYEzjHiY+x8VbzRvXhYnLQBfDIFg1zKGQNSf4nl0gxxOFmJC81MA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('knGbX7yZeeK1Be3a7QdQLRmMGOnddEyqTR+Tf2E5S/sKPOXtTr9f0xJ/4Rsw9aq5IJOnpDDvcJMl0moKfdH3RA==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer18120865654218753494">Susane Colasanti is the bestselling author of <i>When It Happens</i>, <i>Take Me There</i>, <i>Waiting for You</i>, <i>Something Like Fate</i>, <i>So Much Closer</i>, <i>Keep Holding On</i>, <i>All I Need</i>, <i>Now and Forever</i>, and the City Love trilogy. She has a bachelor’s degree from the University of Pennsylvania and a master’s degree from New York University. Before becoming a full-time author in 2007, Susane was a high school science teache</span>
  <span id="freeText18120865654218753494" style="display:none">Susane Colasanti is the bestselling author of <i>When It Happens</i>, <i>Take Me There</i>, <i>Waiting for You</i>, <i>Something Like Fate</i>, <i>So Much Closer</i>, <i>Keep Holding On</i>, <i>All I Need</i>, <i>Now and Forever</i>, and the City Love trilogy. She has a bachelor’s degree from the University of Pennsylvania and a master’s degree from New York University. Before becoming a full-time author in 2007, Susane was a high school science teacher for ten years. She lives in New York City. <br /><br />You can connect with Susane on her <a href="http://www.facebook.com/susanecolasantibooks" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a>, <a href="http://twitter.com/susanecolasanti" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a>, <a href="http://www.youtube.com/user/susanecolasanti" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a>, <a href="http://colasantibooks.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a>, and <a href="https://instagram.com/susanecolasanti" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a>.<br /></span>
